/_next/image?url=%2Fimages%2Fblog%2Fcustomer-story-gamma%2Fcustomer-story-gamma.webp&amp;w=1200&amp;q=75&amp;dpl=dpl_tUd4FNzXLVwprbkNniXcCi3bcFy9 1200w, /_next/image?url=%2Fimages%2Fblog%2Fcustomer-story-gamma%2Fcustomer-story-gamma.webp&amp;w=1920&amp;q=75&amp;dpl=dpl_tUd4FNzXLVwprbkNniXcCi3bcFy9 1920w, /_next/image?url=%2Fimages%2Fblog%2Fcustomer-story-gamma%2Fcustomer-story-gamma.webp&amp;w=2048&amp;q=75&amp;dpl=dpl_tUd4FNzXLVwprbkNniXcCi3bcFy9 2048w, /_next/image?url=%2Fimages%2Fblog%2Fcustomer-story-gamma%2Fcustomer-story-gamma.webp&amp;w=3840&amp;q=75&amp;dpl=dpl_tUd4FNzXLVwprbkNniXcCi3bcFy9 3840w" src="/_next/image?url=%2Fimages%2Fblog%2Fcustomer-story-gamma%2Fcustomer-story-gamma.webp&amp;w=3840&amp;q=75&amp;dpl=dpl_tUd4FNzXLVwprbkNniXcCi3bcFy9"/><div class="w-56"></div><div class="prose mt-32"><p><em>Gamma uses Firecrawl to let anyone turn a blog post, Notion page, or any URL into a polished presentation or website — clean markdown on every request, no noise.</em></p>
<p><strong>What is Gamma?</strong> Gamma is an AI-powered design tool used by 50 million people to create stunning presentations, websites, and documents without any coding or design experience.</p>
<p>When you&#x27;re building an AI tool that turns ideas into polished content, input quality determines output quality. Importing web content means dealing with ads, navigation, boilerplate, and noise. Clean, usable text doesn&#x27;t come for free.</p>
<p><a class="!underline" href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/jonnoronha/">Jon Noronha</a>, Co-Founder at <a class="!underline" href="https://gamma.app/">Gamma</a>, and his team built the platform to let anyone create presentations and websites as easily as writing a doc. When they launched Gamma Sites, they wanted users to be able to transform existing websites into the Gamma format. That required a reliable way to pull clean content from any URL.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="what-did-gamma-need-firecrawl-to-do?"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5">What did Gamma need Firecrawl to do?</h2></div>
<p>Gamma Sites lets users convert any website into the Gamma format. To make that work, they needed to reliably import web pages and strip out the noise.</p>
<p>Firecrawl solved two problems at once. It enabled web page import for Gamma Sites — and it unlocked a new input for Gamma&#x27;s AI presentation generator. Users can now paste in a blog post, Notion page, or any online document and convert it into a presentation in seconds.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="what-did-the-firecrawl-integration-look-like?"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5">What did the Firecrawl integration look like?</h2></div>
<p>Gamma already uses markdown internally. The integration was straightforward.</p>
<blockquote>
<p>It was just a matter of plugging in the Firecrawl API, feeding it a URL, and getting clean markdown in return.</p>
</blockquote>
<p><em>— Jon Noronha, Co-Founder, Gamma</em></p>
<p>No wrestling with HTML. No stripping boilerplate. Clean content, ready to use.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="what-would-gamma-miss-most-without-firecrawl?"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5">What would Gamma miss most without Firecrawl?</h2></div>
<blockquote>
<p>The simplicity of scraping out all the extraneous content and retrieving just the text and images is what we would miss the most if we had to stop using Firecrawl.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>That simplicity is what makes the feature work at scale. Throughout the integration, the Firecrawl team was quick to respond to feature requests and ensured a smooth experience.</p>
<hr/>
<p><strong>Ready to power your AI application with reliable web data?</strong> <a class="!underline" href="https://www.firecrawl.dev">Try Firecrawl</a> and ship faster.</p></div></div></div><div class="flex flex-col lg:py-72 py-40 px-24 mx-auto max-w-800 w-full"><h2 class="text-title-h5 text-accent-black mb-32">Frequently Asked Questions</h2><div class="prose"><div><h3>How does Gamma use Firecrawl?</h3><p>Gamma uses Firecrawl in two ways: to let users transform existing websites into the Gamma format for Gamma Sites, and to power their AI presentation generator by importing any URL — blog posts, Notion pages, or online documents — as clean markdown.</p></div><div><h3>What made the Firecrawl integration easy for Gamma?</h3><p>Gamma already uses markdown internally, so integration was straightforward — plug in the Firecrawl API, feed it a URL, and get clean markdown in return.</p></div><div><h3>What would Gamma miss most without Firecrawl?</h3><p>The simplicity of scraping out all the extraneous content and retrieving just the text and images. That reliability is what makes the feature work at scale for 50M+ users.</p></div></div></div><div class="h-42 p-30 border-t border-border-faint relative lg-max:hidden"><svg fill="none" height="21" from the web into structured data much more quickly.**\n\nWe've rebuilt Firecrawl's PDF parsing engine from the ground up. The new Rust-based parser is up to **3x faster** and more reliable across every document type.\n\n## What's new in PDF Parser v2\n\n**Rust-based parser for significantly faster extraction**\n\nThe previous PDF extraction engine has been replaced with a new Rust-based system. Parsing is now up to 3x faster, which matters when you're ingesting large document sets, building knowledge bases, or parsing AI agents with fresh data in real time.\n\n**Three parsing modes, built for every document type**\n\nYou can now choose how Firecrawl processes PDFs based on your workload:\n\n- **Fast**: pure text extraction using the Rust parser. Best for clean, text-based PDFs where speed is the priority.\n- **Auto**: the new default. Attempts fast extraction first, then automatically falls back to OCR if text extraction fails or returns incomplete results. Works across any PDF type without manual retries.\n- **OCR**: forces full OCR parsing. Designed for scanned documents, image-only PDFs, and files with complex encodings or embedded graphics.\n\n**Reliable extraction across complex layouts**\n\nAuto mode handles the edge cases that break traditional parsers, including charts, tables, mixed encodings, and multi-column layouts, so you can trust results without inspecting every document manually.\n\n## How it works\n\nBy default, Firecrawl uses **Auto mode** when scraping PDFs, with no code changes required for existing users. You can also specify a mode explicitly using the `parsePDF` parameter:\n\n```python\nfrom firecrawl import Firecrawl\n\nfirecrawl = Firecrawl(api_key='fc-YOUR_API_KEY')\n\n# Auto mode (default): fast extraction with automatic OCR fallback\nresult = firecrawl.scrape(\n    url='https://example.com/annual-report.pdf',\n    formats=['markdown'],\n    parsePDF='auto'\n)\n\n# Fast mode: Rust-based text extraction only\nresult = firecrawl.scrape(\n    url='https://example.com/document.pdf',\n    formats=['markdown'],\n    parsePDF='fast'\n)\n\n# OCR mode: for scanned or image-only PDFs\nresult = firecrawl.scrape(\n    url='https://example.com/scanned-filing.pdf',\n    formats=['markdown'],\n    parsePDF='ocr'\n)\n\n```\n\n## Use cases\n\n**AI agents and knowledge bases**\n\nAI agents can now ingest technical papers, product manuals, and scanned reports with greater completeness and speed. More accurate extraction means richer knowledge bases, with fewer gaps in embedded text, tables, or structured data, so agents reason over more complete information.\n\n**AI search and deep research**\n\nPDF-heavy sources like whitepapers, regulatory filings, and research datasets are indexed faster across complex layouts or OCR-dependent content. Better embeddings, higher retrieval accuracy, and faster time-to-insight at scale.\n\n**Data and market intelligence**\n\nReports and filings locked inside PDFs are now extracted at production speed with higher accuracy. Teams running real-time competitive, financial, or industry monitoring get cleaner data, with fewer missed fields and fewer distorted results flowing into downstream analytics.\n\n## Start using PDF Parser v2\n\nPDF Parser v2 is available now. Agents and the sites they visit are fully contained within the sandbox, so you can run code securely without risk to your own infrastructure.\n\nSince nothing runs locally, there are no CPU or RAM spikes on your machine. And you can launch parallel sessions - each in its own sandbox - scaling from one browser to hundreds without managing anything.\n\n### Zero config, pre-loaded with the tools agents already use\n\nBrowser Sandbox comes pre-loaded with Playwright and Agent Browser, so your agents have everything they need to interact with the web. No Chromium to install, no browser framework to configure.\n\nCompatible with Claude Code, Codex, OpenCode, and more.\n\n### Persistent or temporary sessions - you choose\n\nPersistent sessions let you create profiles where auth and state carry across runs. Your agents can pick up where they left off - no re-logging in, no re-navigating. Ideal for workflows that span multiple sessions or require saved credentials.\n\nTemporary sessions are the opposite: clean, disposable browsers that spin up fresh every time. Perfect for one-off extracts where you don't need any state to carry over.\n\n### Fully interactive\n\nBrowser sessions are fully interactive. You can click around alongside your agents, watching what they do and stepping in when you need to.\n\n### Scrape, search, and browse - all through Firecrawl\n\nBrowser Sandbox works alongside Firecrawl's existing scrape and search endpoints. This installs the CLI, authenticates through the browser, and adds the Firecrawl skill to all your agents.\n\n## The Problem: Agents Need Better Web Data\n\nMost agents rely on web fetch tools that break on JavaScript-heavy sites, miss key content, or return unusable HTML. When they do get data, they dump entire pages into context, wasting tokens and slowing down reasoning.\n\nThe Firecrawl [CLI](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/why-clis-are-better-for-agents) and Skill helps AI agents reliably access real-time web data on their own. With a single install, agents like Claude Code, Antigravity, and OpenCode can access all of your favorite Firecrawl endpoints - including scrape, search, crawl, and map for any use case you need.\n\n## Meet Firecrawl CLI\n\n[Firecrawl CLI](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/sdks/cli) is a command-line tool designed for agents and developers who need **reliable web data.**\n\n### Core Commands\n\n- **scrape** - Pull clean markdown from any page, even JavaScript-heavy sites\n- **crawl** - Follow links recursively and gather content from an entire site\n- **map** - Discover all URLs on a domain for comprehensive coverage\n- **search** - Search the web and scrape the results in one step\n\n### Context-Efficient Data for Agents\n\nFirecrawl CLI uses a file-based approach for context management and bash methods for efficient search and retrieval.\n\n### Industry-Leading Reliability\n\n[Firecrawl delivers \u003e80% coverage on benchmark evaluations](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/the-worlds-best-web-data-api-v25) - outperforming every other provider tested. It handles JavaScript rendering, dynamic content, authentication flows, and complex page structures that break other scrapers.\n\n*(Methodology: Checked 1,000 URLs for content recall and whether various tools in the market retrieved at least 10% of the expected content gap, using the [Firecrawl scrape-content-dataset-v1 dataset](https://huggingface.co/datasets/firecrawl/scrape-content-dataset-v1).)*\n\n**Example usage:**\n\n```bash\n# Scrape a page to markdown\n$ firecrawl scrape https://example.com/pricing --format markdown -o pricing.md\n\n# Crawl an entire website, wait for completion, and output results\n$ firecrawl crawl https://example.com --wait --progress -o example-crawl.json\n\n# Map an entire domain\n$ firecrawl map https://example.com -o sitemap.json\n\n# Search and scrape top results\n$ firecrawl search \"AI agent benchmarks 2026\" --scrape --limit 5 -o results/\n```\n\nAll results are written to the filesystem, so agents can search, analyze, or process data locally.\n\n## Firecrawl Skill: Teach Agents to Use the CLI\n\nThe Firecrawl Skill is a skill package that teaches AI agents how to install, authenticate, and use Firecrawl CLI - end to end.\n\nSkills are declarative packages that agents can install via the `npx skills` protocol. Once installed, agents know how to use the tool without manual integration.\n\n### What the Skill Teaches\n\n1. How to install Firecrawl CLI\n2. How to authenticate with an API key\n3. When and how to use scrape, map, and search commands\n4. How to structure output for efficient filesystem usage\n\n### Coding Agent Harness Compatibility\n\nThe Firecrawl Skill works with any agent that supports the Skills protocol:\n\n- **Claude Code** — Agentic coding in your terminal\n- **OpenAI Codex** — Build with GPT-4 in the CLI\n- **Gemini CLI** — Google's agent interface\n- **OpenCode** — Open-source agent harness\n- And more\n\nOne skill, every major coding agent harness.\n\n### Why Skills Matter\n\nYou don't configure endpoints, handle auth, or write tool definitions. The Skill does it. Add Firecrawl once, and your agent knows how to use it forever.\n\nAs the Skill evolves, your agent learns new capabilities automatically. No code changes. No redeployment. It just works. If you want to build your own [Claude Code automation skill](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/claude-code-skill) for a custom tool or workflow, we have a step-by-step tutorial that covers the full structure from scratch.\n\n## Firecrawl CLI + Skill: Agents Empowered with Live Web Data\n\nWhen you combine Firecrawl CLI with our skill, your agent can reliably access web data on its own.\n\n### How It Works\n\n1. You run `$ npx -y firecrawl-cli@latest init --all --browser`\n2. The skill teaches your agent about Firecrawl CLI capabilities\n3. When your agent needs web data, it installs and uses the CLI automatically\n4. Results are written to the filesystem, not dumped into context\n5. Your agent searches, analyzes, or processes the data locally\n\nHere's a quick look at common use cases where agents with Firecrawl shine:\n\n| Use case | Value |\n| --- | --- |\n| **Competitor product research** | Track pricing, feature pages, and changes across competitor sites - so you get fresh data on specs, updates, and positioning without manual checking |\n| **Documentation and help centers** | Pull full docs and help centers for the latest information, giving agents current API references and guides instead of stale training data |\n| **Site change monitoring** | Detect updates across large sites, from pricing shifts to new content, and map entire domains to track changes over time automatically |\n| **Deep research with sources** | Collect structured sources with URLs and timestamps to ground answers in verifiable data with proper attribution |\n\n## Get Started\n\nInstall the Firecrawl CLI and skill in all your agents:\n\n```bash\n$ npx -y firecrawl-cli@latest init --all --browser\n```\n\nOr use the CLI directly:\n\n```bash\n$ npm install -g firecrawl-cli\n$ firecrawl auth --api-key fc-YOUR_KEY\n$ firecrawl scrape https://example.com\n```\n\n[Check out our docs for more info.](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/sdks/cli)\n\nGive your agent the best web data available. A chatbot that hallucinates can cost huge $$$. An agent making decisions with stale data or broken sources can be business-critical.\n\n[Jack Fischer](https://www.linkedin.com/in/jackfischer11/), Co-Founder \u0026 CTO of [Credal](https://www.credal.ai/), and his team understand this very well. They've built a platform that lets companies deploy AI agents with strict access controls, comprehensive audit trails, and, crucially, the ability to pull in fresh external context when needed.\n\n\u003e We run production agent workflows where the model needs either fresh external context or non-standard data without ETL. Our customers need their agents to reference today's facts or pull from their customer-facing support docs without building a custom integration.\n\n*— Jack Fischer, Co-Founder \u0026 CTO, Credal*\n\n## Why does web data need two different approaches?\n\nCredal's architecture treats web data differently depending on the use case:\n\n- **\"Web search\" (ephemeral)**: Fetch a handful of relevant pages for this specific conversation, show the links as sources, and move on. The agent needs to know what happened at yesterday's press conference or check current API documentation.\n\n- **\"Webpages ingestion\" (durable)**: Crawl an entire site, snapshot the content, and push it through Credal's indexing + retrieval + citations pipeline, the same infrastructure they use for internal sources like Confluence or Google Drive.\n\nThis split keeps the UX honest. Users can see exactly what the model looked at, right now. And it delivers on Credal's product promise: easily [crawl any URL](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/crawl) into your knowledge base without code.\n\nBut implementing this dual approach meant solving some hard technical problems.\n\n## What makes \"LLM-ready\" content so hard?\n\n\u003eOur ingestion and retrieval stack expects clean text. We need a stable way to turn messy HTML into markdown we can snapshot, embed, and cite.\n\nAnyone who's tried to extract usable content from the modern web knows this isn't trivial. [JavaScript-rendered content](https://www.firecrawl.dev/glossary/web-scraping-apis/what-is-javascript-rendering-web-scraping), nested navigation structures, ads, cookie banners, duplicate boilerplate: the list goes on. And when you're processing millions of pages monthly, edge cases become routine cases.\n\nCredal integrated Firecrawl specifically for its reliable markdown extraction. \n\nThe content that comes back is already normalized, which means it flows directly into their vector indexing pipeline without additional cleanup.\n\n## How do you turn site crawling into a product feature?\n\nThe second critical capability: recursive site crawling that works at production scale.\n\n\u003eWe don't just scrape single pages. We support recursive site crawls that land as a folder-like object in our system, with per-page snapshots and vector indexing.\n\nWhen a customer adds their documentation site to Credal, they expect it to \"just work\": discover all the pages, handle rate limits gracefully, manage timeouts, normalize the content, and index everything for retrieval. Building this from scratch means reinventing solutions to problems that Firecrawl has already solved through hard-earned edge-case handling.\n\n\u003eIf we lost Firecrawl, we could replace search discovery relatively quickly. But replacing scrape + crawl + normalization at production quality? That's what would hurt.\n\n## What does production-ready actually mean?\n\nCredal's integration reflects their enterprise DNA. They built assuming production realities: timeouts, partial failures, load spikes. They added their own health checks, logging, and rate limits to make the system debuggable and reliable.\n\nThe result: **6 million+ URLs scraped monthly**, powering AI agents that enterprises actually trust with business-critical workflows.\n\nFor companies building AI products where reliability isn't optional, Credal offers a blueprint: focus on your differentiation (secure agent orchestration, access controls, audit trails) and lean on specialized tools for the undifferentiated heavy lifting.\n\nAs Jack puts it: \n\n\u003eWe scrape more than 6M URLs a month for our users' agents without any web scraping code.\n\n---\n\n**Ready to power your AI application with reliable web data?** [Try Firecrawl](\u003chttps://www.firecrawl.dev\u003e) and ship faster.\n\n"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"a5:Tebf,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"\nToday we're launching **Spark 1 Pro** and **Spark 1 Mini** — two new models powering [`/agent`](http://firecrawl.dev/agent), our most loved endpoint that searches, navigates, and extracts web data from a single prompt.\n\n- **Spark 1 Mini** is 60% cheaper and handles most extraction tasks with solid accuracy.\n- **Spark 1 Pro** delivers exceptional recall for complex, multi-step research.\n\nTogether, they make `/agent` our most powerful and flexible extraction endpoint yet.\n\n## Why two models?\n\nWeb extraction isn't one-size-fits-all. Contact information is buried across company sites, team pages, and press releases.\n\nResearching pricing? Competitors hide their pricing behind multi-page flows, gated content, or dynamic tables.\n\nCurating datasets? The data you need is scattered - research papers across publishers, company information across databases, product specs across e-commerce sites.\n\nTraditional web scraping requires you to map every site structure, write custom code for each page type, and maintain brittle scripts when layouts change. It's slow, expensive, and breaks constantly.\n\nYou need a better way to gather data at scale.\n\n## How /agent works\n\nDescribe what data you want to extract and /agent handles the rest.\n\n```python\nfrom firecrawl import FirecrawlApp\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel, Field\nfrom typing import List, Optional\n\napp = FirecrawlApp(api_key=\"fc-YOUR_API_KEY\")\n\nclass Company(BaseModel):\n    name: str = Field(description=\"Company name\")\n    contact_email: Optional[str] = Field(None, description=\"Contact email\")\n    employee_count: Optional[str] = Field(None, description=\"Number of employees\")\n\nclass CompaniesSchema(BaseModel):\n    companies: List[Company] = Field(description=\"List of companies\")\n\nresult = app.agent(\n    prompt=\"Find YC W24 dev tool companies and get their contact info and team size\",\n    schema=CompaniesSchema\n)\n\nprint(result.data)\n```\n\nNo URLs required. Retell ships with a built-in [Knowledge Base](https://www.retellai.com/features/knowledge-base) that ingests URLs, files, and custom text so agents use the same sources human teams trust.\n\nAs larger customers came on with multi-product documentation and JavaScript-heavy portals, each new account meant another fragile scraper and another round of \"did we miss this page?\" debugging.\n\n## What was the old, traditional approach costing Retell?\n\nKeeping knowledge bases current meant maintaining a mix of one-off Puppeteer/Playwright scripts, sitemap crawls, and manual copy-paste from docs sites. They could wire bespoke scrapers for each account, rely on occasional exports and sitemaps, or accept that some calls would route through outdated answers.\n\nThese setups shipped, but they did not meet the bar Retell sets for call containment and cost per call.\n\nWhat they wanted instead was a straightforward pipeline from documentation to LLM-ready content. A knowledge base they could treat as configuration, not a new engineering project every time a customer signed. Firecrawl's web scraping API, already powering more than 40,000 knowledge bases, fills that gap.\n\n## How does Firecrawl fit into the knowledge base pipeline of Retell?\n\nRetell now standardizes on Firecrawl's [/scrape](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/scrape) endpoint as the ingestion primitive behind these knowledge bases.\n\n[Firecrawl](https://www.firecrawl.dev/use-cases/ai-chats) takes a docs URL, an API reference, changelog, status page, or support center, and turns it into LLM-ready markdown or JSON. Navigation, boilerplate, and ad-like clutter are stripped out.\n\nBacked by Firecrawl's [Fire-Engine](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/introducing-fire-engine-for-firecrawl) browser layer, it handles JavaScript-heavy docs and PDFs without Retell running its own headless browser fleet or proxy rotation.\n\nInstead of writing a new scraper for every customer, the team defines small, focused scrape jobs around the URLs that actually matter. Firecrawl handles pagination, navigation, and rendering. The output drops into the embedding and retrieval stack that already powers their agents.\n\nExtending coverage is a matter of adding a URL to a Firecrawl job, not re-architecting ingestion.\n\nAs they rolled Firecrawl into production, the team experimented with different endpoints. They used [/map](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/map) to understand docs structures and [/scrape](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/scrape) to hydrate the content itself. Leading with targeted scrape jobs on a short list of each customer's docs and help center links gave them the predictable coverage they needed for voice agents.\n\nTogether with the Firecrawl team, they documented a clear pattern, with guidance on where [/batch-scrape](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/batch-scrape), [/crawl](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/crawl), and [/map](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/map) make sense for larger, multi-domain documentation sets.\n\n## What does the production pattern look like for Retell?\n\nFor each new customer, Retell keeps a short list of docs and help center links as configuration for Firecrawl jobs, instead of hard-coding them into bespoke scripts.\n\nWhen a job works well for one account, for example scraping a multi-language API reference plus changelog, it becomes a template Retell can reuse across that vertical.\n\nRefreshing a knowledge base means rerunning Firecrawl jobs or adjusting their config, not touching scraping infrastructure. This release represents a significant leap forward in web data extraction, powered by two major infrastructure improvements: our new Semantic Index and a completely custom browser stack.\n\n## A Custom Browser Stack Built for Quality\n\nTo achieve maximum data quality, we built our own browser stack from the ground up. This wasn't a decision we made lightly, but the results speak for themselves.\n\nOur custom browser stack automatically detects how each page is rendered, allowing us to extract data at high speeds while maintaining an exceptionally high quality bar. The browser fleet is designed to handle any content type (PDFs, paginated tables, dynamic JavaScript applications) and convert them into clean, agent-ready formats that work seamlessly with AI systems.\n\nThis architecture enables us to index complete pages rather than partial content, which is critical for maintaining data integrity. The impact on quality is substantial, as demonstrated in our benchmarks against leading competitors:\n\n![Firecrawl v2.5 Quality Benchmarks](/images/blog/v25/firecrawl25benchmarksquality.webp)\n\n## Introducing Our Semantic Index\n\nAlongside our custom browser stack, we've built a semantic index that fundamentally improves both coverage and speed. This index already serves 40% of all API calls, enabling us to deliver top-tier data quickly across most websites.\n\nThe semantic index contains previously captured full page snapshots, embeddings, and structural metadata. This allows us to offer a unique capability: users can request data \"as of now\" or \"as of last known good copy,\" effectively providing access to any previous or current state of the web at any moment. You can control this behavior using the `maxAge` parameter, which lets you specify how recent the data should be.\n\nThis dual-mode approach ensures both reliability and freshness, giving developers the flexibility to choose the right data retrieval strategy for their use case.
